<div id="review_2295861141" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2295861141" />
    <a title="Mounir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/348979-mounir"><img alt="Mounir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485779406p2/348979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2295861141?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mounir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mounir" href="/user/show/348979-mounir">Mounir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/38579035-baltasar-and-blimunda">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/348979-mounir?shelf=literature-portuguese">literature-portuguese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/348979-mounir?shelf=a-english-translation">a-english-translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295861141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7398348930416490818">(المراجعة باللغة العربية إلى أسفل)<br/>Each novel by Jose Saramago is a masterpiece, including this historical tale from 18th century Portugal, with tells of two actual building projects: the story of the building of Mafra palace and convent(hence the original title: Memorial do Convento); the king's vanity and absolute power; the hundreds of men and women involved in this huge - and useless - project; the lives lost; the persons maimed; the families disrupted; all for a promise made by a king to the</span>
  <span id="freeText7398348930416490818" style="display:none">(المراجعة باللغة العربية إلى أسفل)<br />Each novel by Jose Saramago is a masterpiece, including this historical tale from 18th century Portugal, with tells of two actual building projects: the story of the building of Mafra palace and convent(hence the original title: Memorial do Convento); the king's vanity and absolute power; the hundreds of men and women involved in this huge - and useless - project; the lives lost; the persons maimed; the families disrupted; all for a promise made by a king to the Franciscan order. And don't forget the Inquisition. <br />On the other hand, there is the building of a Flying Machine, a primitive scientific attempt at flying, done only by three persons. <br />Saramago tells these stories in his usual distinctive style, here with elements from historical and mythical tales, mixing historical fact with fiction and with some magical or supernatural elements; and as usual with bitter sarcasm of the royal concern with glory and pomp, and of the tedious ceremonies of church people and friars, without forgetting to expose the religious hypocrisy of ordinary people.<br />And among all of all this, there is the tender love story; and there remains only the simple facts: tenderness, real emotions, human warmth, and love. <br />روايات جوزيه ساراماجو كلها تعتبر من روائع الأعمال، بما فيها هذه الرواية عن البرتغال في القرن الثامن عشر، التي يحكي فيها عن مشروعين حقيقيين للبناء: القصر الملكي والدير بمدينة مافرا (ومن هنا العنوان الأصلي للرواية: مذكرات الدير)، وغرور الملك واستبداده، ومئات الرجال والنساء الذين تأثرت حياتهم بهذا المشروع الضخم قليل الفائدة؛ أشخاص فقدوا حياتهم أو تشوهوا، عائلات تفككت، وكل ذلك من أجل تنفيذ ما وعده الملك للرهبان الفرنسيسكان. وبالإضافة إلى ذلك هناك محاكم التفتيش.<br />وفي مقابل ذلك، هناك قصة أخرى حقيقية عن محاولة بناء آلة تطير في الهواء، محاولة علمية بدائية قام بها ثلاث أشخاص فقط.<br />يحكي ساراماجو كل ذلك بأسلوبه المميز، مع إضافة عناصر أسلوبية من النصوص التاريخية والأسطورية، مازجا بين الحقيقة التاريخية والخيال، ومع بعض العناصر السحرية. وكعادته، هناك سخرية مرة من انشغال الملك وحاشيته بالمجد والمظاهر والأبهة، وسخرية من الطقوس الكنسية الثقيلة، ولا ينسى أن يسخر من النفاق والرياء الديني لجموع الناس.<br />ووسط كل ذلك، هناك قصة الحب الرقيقة، حيث لا يبقى في النهاية إلا الحقائق البسيطة: الحنان، والمشاعر الحقيقية، والدفء الإنساني، والحب</span>
  <a data-text-id="7398348930416490818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer18172683152454891287">Set in the backdrop of Lisbon during the 18th century Portuguese inquisition is a love story between two peasants: Baltasar, a war veteran with a hook for a hand and Blimunda, with her ability to literally see inside of people. Throw in a Brazilian priest (based on the historical figure of Bartolomeu de Gusmão) with a flying machine and you have some of the most delicious magical realism out there that's tempered with historical splashes that ground this book. These include bed bug infestations,</span>
  <span id="freeText18172683152454891287" style="display:none">Set in the backdrop of Lisbon during the 18th century Portuguese inquisition is a love story between two peasants: Baltasar, a war veteran with a hook for a hand and Blimunda, with her ability to literally see inside of people. Throw in a Brazilian priest (based on the historical figure of Bartolomeu de Gusmão) with a flying machine and you have some of the most delicious magical realism out there that's tempered with historical splashes that ground this book. These include bed bug infestations, a plague, auto da fés, and banishment to Algeria for witchcraft. Saramago's writing is Shakespearean in depth, irony, and beauty. Both philosophical and passionate, dark and beautiful a very "good read". </span>

  <span id="freeText3413647355855535951" style="display:none">With some books the chemistry just doesn't work and this is one of them. From page 1 the exuberant, baroque, antiquated language is flowing out of the book: impossible long sentences, with lots of appositions and neverending descriptions; it's all too artificial for me. <br /><br />The setting, Portugal in the beginning of the 18th century, and the love story that is at the center of this book, are quite interesting. <span id="freeTextContainer10000250997567916165">Sarramago's writing, which foregoes the normal stylistic emphasis on the change from one character's voice to another (quotes and new paragraphs), allows us to view them all collectively rather than having the 'camera' zoom in on each speaker in turn. This communal effect brings the reader into immediate and intimate contact with the characters. This story, in particular, tells of such a compelling love that the magical realism of the characters appears to be the only way to do it justice. As al</span>
  <span id="freeText10000250997567916165" style="display:none">Sarramago's writing, which foregoes the normal stylistic emphasis on the change from one character's voice to another (quotes and new paragraphs), allows us to view them all collectively rather than having the 'camera' zoom in on each speaker in turn. This communal effect brings the reader into immediate and intimate contact with the characters. This story, in particular, tells of such a compelling love that the magical realism of the characters appears to be the only way to do it justice. As always, the commentary woven into the narrative is inescapable and sharp.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_463127965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/463127965" />
    <a title="Drilona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5847852-drilona"><img alt="Drilona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529250049p2/5847852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/463127965?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drilona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drilona" href="/user/show/5847852-drilona">Drilona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5847852-drilona?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463127965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8588189480508924989">This was one of the most tantalizing books I've ever read. I bought this one at the book fair last month, as I had heard many people praise Saramango's works. Meanwhile, I knew nothing about his style of writing, nor had I read any of his books.<br/><br/>So I started reading 'Baltasar and Blimunda', unaware of what I was going through. Long sentences, weird dialogue; sometimes I couldn't get who said what. There were times I had to read over the same page twice! After I read the first thirty pages, I knew</span>
  <span id="freeText8588189480508924989" style="display:none">This was one of the most tantalizing books I've ever read. I bought this one at the book fair last month, as I had heard many people praise Saramango's works. Meanwhile, I knew nothing about his style of writing, nor had I read any of his books.<br /><br />So I started reading 'Baltasar and Blimunda', unaware of what I was going through. Long sentences, weird dialogue; sometimes I couldn't get who said what. There were times I had to read over the same page twice! After I read the first thirty pages, I knew this was not going to be easy to read, but I had a feeling that i was going to like it. Even though I consider it weird, I liked this book very much. It's the best love story I've ever read.<br />I like to think of it as Saramango's 'Bible', or maybe his 'Divine Comedy'. It's as allegorical as those two books: It's inspiring, smart, and touching in a non-religious way. I don't get all of its symbolism, but I do understand a few things in my own way, though.<br /><br />It looks like the symbols based on numbers are inevitable when it comes to these kind of books. For example, number 7, Baltasar is also called Seven-Suns and Blimunda, Seven-Moons. From what I read, I think they were seven years apart. Number 9, at the end, Blimunda searched for Baltasar for nine long years, 9 are the gifts of the spirit which i think Blimunda revealed along those years. There's also the number 3; the trinity, Baltasar- Bartolomeu de Gusmao-Blimunda. It could be that Blimunda represents the Holy Spirit as she could see through people, Baltasar might be God, according to what Bartolomeu says. God also had only one hand.<br /><br />While the flying machine might be their son, it is somehow their creation (Baltasar and Blimunda never had a child, while for years they took care of the machine). Father Bartolomeu represents the Church and Gospel, but a different church and Gospel of course as this Trinity has nothing to do with the one we know. About the religion; it is suppressing and based on hypocrisy.<br />I find my thoughts in Bartolomeu's words, "...He came to be inside man, so man is virtually God, or will ultimately become God, yes, of course, if God resides in me, I am God, I am God not in Triune or quadruple, but one, one with God, He is, I am He...". Even thought the book was set in the 18th century, I guess it fits even nowadays. There was a king with a whim and the folk who died to fulfill it. Isn't it the same for today? There are still kings and popes. Don't we do what we are told to do, willingly or unwillingly!? <br /><br />Anyway, as I said, what I liked the most about this book was the love story between Baltasar and Blimunda. Baltasar is not perfect, but he completes Blimunda. There's nothing wrong with Blimunda but yet she's happy with someone like Baltasar! I've come to think You shouldn't marry at all if she can't see though people or collect wills. You shouldn't marry at all if he has both hands or can't build a flying machine!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8588189480508924989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/707951282?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those of you who are fond of the classics and don't mind a strange form of writing</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015317-mariana?shelf=historical-novels">historical-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015317-mariana?shelf=you-cannot-mistreat-the-classics">you-cannot-mistreat-the-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015317-mariana?shelf=author-jose-saramago">author-jose-saramago</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015317-mariana?shelf=i-actually-fell-asleep">i-actually-fell-asleep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015317-mariana?shelf=school-readings">school-readings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015317-mariana?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer707951282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4197066412140143088"><b>3 stars</b><br/><br/>I confess my expectations weren't very high for this book. People always ranted about how boring it would be, and I believed them.<br/><br/>I actually enjoyed the "Memorial". Yes, it is a historical romance situated in the eighteenth century's prejudiced and excessively religious Portugal, but it is also the portrayal of a love of cosmical proportions, the world's first flying machine, the extenuating construction of the Convent of Mafra, the barbarities committed by the world-famous Inquisition, t</span>
  <span id="freeText4197066412140143088" style="display:none"><b>3 stars</b><br /><br />I confess my expectations weren't very high for this book. People always ranted about how boring it would be, and I believed them.<br /><br />I actually enjoyed the "Memorial". Yes, it is a historical romance situated in the eighteenth century's prejudiced and excessively religious Portugal, but it is also the portrayal of a love of cosmical proportions, the world's first flying machine, the extenuating construction of the Convent of Mafra, the barbarities committed by the world-famous Inquisition, the vanity of a king... <br /><br />I especially adored the humorous moments filled with irony that you can find in these dense pages, like for instance how every nun in every single religious order in Lisbon wasn't God's wife, but the king's/the ordinary man's mistress.<br /><br />Focusing on the very polemic topic of Saramago's writing style, I got used to it very quickly and didn't find it disturbing at all. His way of organising sentences and dialogues is very creative and, after about a dozen pages, easy to follow.<br /><br />All in all, this was an acceptable book, which I managed to appreciate, yet I did not love it. Instead, I found it a bit slow at times, which led to many pauses on my part, hence the rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4197066412140143088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697354883?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/8311987-david">David</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697354883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9781753591580885274">I loved the first half of the book immensely, the story of Baltasar, Blimunda, their love and struggles, her mysterious gift/curse, and their dealings with the curious Padré and the harpsichord player. However, it took me a long time to get through the second half of this book which focused on the construction of the Palace at Mafra, and I had a hard time deciding whether to give it a three or a four. Perhaps a 3.5 would be best, though the ending may have bumped it up to a four. I imagine if I </span>
  <span id="freeText9781753591580885274" style="display:none">I loved the first half of the book immensely, the story of Baltasar, Blimunda, their love and struggles, her mysterious gift/curse, and their dealings with the curious Padré and the harpsichord player. However, it took me a long time to get through the second half of this book which focused on the construction of the Palace at Mafra, and I had a hard time deciding whether to give it a three or a four. Perhaps a 3.5 would be best, though the ending may have bumped it up to a four. I imagine if I were Portuguese I might have enjoyed or at least been able to relate to the history more (though I must admit that I do now have a desire to see the Palace in Mafra as a result of reading the book). I've grown accustomed to Saramago's style, and he truly is a master of words, some of the paragraphs he writes are simply blissful. I will continue to read his work, all of it in time, I expect: and while this was not a favorite, it was a worthy book in and of itself.</span>

  <span id="freeText6806733868957385534" style="display:none">I read Blindness as a starry-eyed 18 year old youth, and loved it loved it loved it. As spare as Blindness was, Baltasar and Blimunda is rich and dense.<br /><br />There's some beautiful imagery here. The problem is that the Baroque-styled writing-- while amusing at first-- eventually starts to grate a bit. But the story itself is so lovely that I was willing to bare through it. I can't hate.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JGMg3A95wU1IUqqrt4CxDOBz5F2S2KPTe+DUhqVk8f8eRUkOtCcIJe95HspAdbvTNiwDlVxVLbQgnpI3aCcDZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MPDxLxzg5HwKc4+b5EisOUS8Fh5xze6MoFRzO7wLYOYK1pj9p74tFK1YO/oTvabmkuPx1r9AYOv7KjWKcUiSfA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_1249630'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1249630.Os_Maias?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Os Maias<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/6913270.E_a_de_Queir_s?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Eça de Queirós<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.02 avg rating &mdash; 17,225 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1888\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer9535265668027654090\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #15\n\nOs Maias é uma das obras mais conhecidas do escritor português Eça de Queiroz. O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresent<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9535265668027654090\" style=\"display:none\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #15\n\nOs Maias é uma das obras mais conhecidas do escritor português Eça de Queiroz. O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresenta-nos a história de três gerações da família Maia. A acção inicia-se no Outono de 1875, quando Afonso da Maia, nobre e pobre proprietário, se instala no Ramalhete com o neto recém formado em Medicina. Neste momento faz-se uma longa descrição da casa - &quot;O Ramalhete,&quot; cujo nome tem origem num painel de azulejos com um ramo de girassóis, e não em algo fresco ou campestre, tal como o nome nos remete a pensar. Afonso da Maia era o personagem mais simpático do romance e aquele que o autor mais valorizou, pois não se lhe conhecem defeitos. É um homem de carácter, culto e requintado nos gostos. Em jovem aderiu aos ideais do Liberalismo e foi obrigado, por seu pai, a sair de casa e a instalar-se em Inglaterra. Após o pai falecer regressa a Lisboa para casar com Maria Eduarda Runa, mas pouco tempo depois escolhe o exílio por razões de ordem política. Há em Os Maias um retrato da Lisboa da epóca. Carlos, que mora na Rua das Janelas Verdes, caminha com frequência até ao Rossio (embora, por vezes, vá a cavalo ou de carruagem). Algumas das lojas citadas no livro ainda existem - a Casa Havaneza, no Chiado, por exemplo. É possível seguir os diferentes percursos de Carlos ou do Ega pelas suas da Baixa lisboeta, ainda que algumas tenham mudado de nome. No final do livro, quando Carlos volta a Lisboa muitos anos depois, somos levados a ver as novidades - a Avenida da Liberdade, que substituiu o Passeio Público, e que é descrita como uma coisa nova, e feia pela sua novidade, exactamente como nos anos 70 se falava das casas de emigrante. O romance veicula sobre o país uma perspectiva muito derrotista, muito pessimista. Tirando a natureza (o Tejo, Sintra, Santa Olávia...), é tudo uma choldra ignóbil. Predomina uma visão de estrangeirado, de quem só valoriza as civilizações superiores - da França e Inglaterra, principalmente. Os políticos são mesquinhos, ignorantes ou corruptos (Gouvarinho, Sousa Neto...); os homens das Letras sao boémios e dissolutos, retrógrados ou distantes da realidade concreta (Alencar, Ega...: lembre-se o que se passou no Sarau do Teatro da Trindade); os jornalistas boémios e venais (Palma...); os homens do desporto não conseguem organizar uma corrida de cavalos, pois não há hipódromo à altura, nem cavalos, nem cavaleiros, as pessoas não vestem como o evento exigia, as senhoras traziam vestidos de missa. Para cúmulo de tudo isto, os protagonistas acabam vencidos da vida. Apesar de ser isto referido no fim do livro, pode-se ver que ainda há alguma esperanca implícita, nas passagens em que Carlos da Maia e João da Ega dizem que o apetite humano é a causa de todos os seus problemas e que portanto nunca mais terão apetites, mas logo a seguir dizem que lhes está a apetecer um &quot;prato de paio com ervilhas,&quot; ou quando dizem que a pressa não leva a nada e que a vida deve ser levada com calma mas começam a correr para apanhar o americano (eléctrico). Mais do que crítica de costumes, o romance mostra-nos um país - sobretudo Lisboa - que se dissolve, incapaz de se regenerar. Quando o autor escreve mais tarde A Cidade e as Serras, expõe uma atitude muito mais construtiva: o protagonista regenera-se pela descoberta das raízes rurais ancestrais não atingidas pela degradação da civilização, num movimento inverso ao que predomina n\'Os Maias.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9535265668027654090\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n adaptado ao teatro – , esta peça contribuiu para celebrizar Luís de Sttau Monteiro como dramaturgo, tendo sido bem recebida pela crítica do seu tempo.\nBaseada na tentativa frustrada de revolta liberal em 1817, supostamente encabeçada por Gomes Freire de Andrade, Felizmente Há Luar! recria em dois actos a sequência de acontecimentos históricos que em Outubro desse ano levou à prisão e ao enforcamento de Gomes Freire pelo regime de Beresford, com o apoio da Igreja, sublinhando um apelo épico (e ético) politicamente empenhado e legível à luz do que era Portugal nos anos 60.\nChamando a atenção para a injustiça da repressão e das perseguições políticas, a peça – designada por &quot;apoteose trágica&quot; pelo Autor – esteve proibida até 1974 e foi pela primeira vez levada à cena apenas em 1978, no Teatro Nacional, numa encenação do próprio Sttau Monteiro.\n\nFonte: http://www.prof2000.pt/users/jsafonso/Port/luar.htm<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6525843189733717470\" //<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_909710'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/909710.Amor_de_Perdi_o?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Amor de Perdição<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/465498.Camilo_Castelo_Branco?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Camilo Castelo Branco<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.54 avg rating &mdash; 5,927 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1862\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer17840695626810635724\">Nas «Memórias do Cárcere», referindo-me ao romance que novamente se imprime, escrevi estas linhas: «O romance, escrito em seguimento daquele («O Romance de um Homem Rico»), foi o «Amor de Perdição». Desde menino, ouvia eu contar a triste história de <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17840695626810635724\" style=\"display:none\">Nas «Memórias do Cárcere», referindo-me ao romance que novamente se imprime, escrevi estas linhas: «O romance, escrito em seguimento daquele («O Romance de um Homem Rico»), foi o «Amor de Perdição». Desde menino, ouvia eu contar a triste história de meu tio paterno Simão António Botelho. Minha tia, irmã dele, solicitada por minha curiosidade, estava sempre pronta a repetir o facto aligado à sua mocidade. Lembrou-me naturalmente, na cadeia, muitas vezes, meu tio, que ali deveria estar inscrito no livro das entradas no cárcere e no das saídas para o degredo. Folheei os livros desde os de 1800, e achei a notícia com pouca fadiga, e alvoroços de contentamento, como se em minha alçada estivesse adornar-lhe a memória como recompensa das suas trágicas e afrontosas dores em vida tão breve. Sabia eu que em casa de minha irmã estavam acantoados uns maços de papéis antigos, tendentes a esclarecer a nebulosa história de meu tio. Pedi aos contemporâneos que o conheceram notícias e miudezas, a fim de entrar de consciência naquele trabalho. Escrevi o romance em quinze dias, os mais atormentados de minha vida. Tão horrorizada tenho deles a memória, que nunca mais abrirei o «Amor de Perdição», nem lhe passarei a lima sobre os defeitos nas edições futuras, se é que não saiu tolhiço incorrigível da primeira. Não sei se lá digo que meu tio Simão chorava, e menos sei se o leitor chorou com ele. De mim lhe juro que…»\nVão passados quase dois anos, depois que protestei não mais abrir este romance. […] Este livro, cujo êxito se me antolhava mau, quando eu o ia escrevendo, teve uma recepção de primazia sobre todos os seus irmãos. Movia-me à desconfiança o ser ele triste, sem interpolação de risos, sombrio, e rematado por catástrofe de confranger o ânimo dos leitores, que se interessam na boa sorte de uns, e no castigo de outros personagens. Em honra e louvor das pessoas que estimaram o meu livro, confessarei agradavelmente que julguei mal delas. […] O livro agradou como está. Seria desacerto e ingratidão demudar sensivelmente, quer na essência, quer na compostura, o que, tal qual é, foi bem recebido.\nDo Prefácio da Segunda Edição. De nome <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16164479244342058287\" style=\"display:none\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #5\n\nJosé Maria de Eça de Queiroz (Póvoa de Varzim, 25 de novembro de 1845 — Neuilly-sur-Seine, 16 de agosto de 1900), escritor e ensaísta, foi um dos nomes mais importantes da literatura portuguesa. De nome completo José Maria de Eça de Queirós nasceu a Novembro de 1845, numa casa na Praça do Almada, em Póvoa de Varzim. O seu pai, José Maria de Almeida de Teixeira de Queirós, nascido no Brasil e vindo para Portugal com um ano de idade, provinha de uma família de magistrados perseguidos pelos seus ideais liberais que defendiam uma doutrina constitucional. Eça foi internado no Colégio da Lapa, no Porto, de onde saiu em 1861, com dezasseis anos, para a Universidade de Coimbra, onde estudou Direito. Num ambiente boémio da cidade universitária de Coimbra estes jovens reuniam-se para trocar ideias, livros e formas para renovar a vida política e cultural portuguesa, que estava a viver uma autêntica revolução social com a introdução dos novos meios de transportes ferroviários que traziam, todos os dias, novidades do centro da Europa, influenciando esta geração para novas ideologias e valores. Foi nesse grupo que Eça conheceu os futuros escritores e poetas, Teófilo Braga, Ramalho Ortigão, Guerra Junqueiro, Guilherme de Azevedo, Oliveira Martins, entre outros; mas sobretudo, foi aí que travou amizade com Antero de Quental, um jovem carismático a quem os membros do grupo chamavam de líder e que incentivou os restantes a seguir e a difundir as então recentes correntes ideológicas e literárias europeias: o Positivismo, o Socialismo e o Realismo-Naturalismo. Notabilizou-se pela originalidade e riqueza do seu estilo e linguagem, nomeadamente pelo realismo descritivo e pela crítica social constantes nos seus romances mas, tal como o crítico literário,       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1285555.Jos_Saramago">About José Saramago</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1285555.Jos_Saramago"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1497455560p3/1285555.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1285555.Jos_Saramago">José Saramago
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
12,208
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer988126068254712039">José Saramago is one of the most important international writers of the last hundred years. Born in Portugal in 1922, he was in his sixties when he came to prominence as a writer with the publication of Baltasar and Blimunda. A huge body of work followed, translated into more than forty languages, and in 1998 he was awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature. Saramago died in June 2010.</span>

</div>
</div>
